On 6 August, the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Mark_Duggan" title="Death of Mark Duggan">Death of Mark Duggan</a> sparked off the <a href="/wiki/2011_England_riots" title="2011 England riots">2011 England riots</a>.\n</p><p>In 2012, the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> returned to London for the first time since 1948. The United States claimed the largest count of gold medals, with Britain running third place after China.\n</p><p>In 2014, Scotland <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence_referendum,_2014" title="Scottish independence referendum, 2014">voted in a referendum</a> on the question of becoming an independent country. The No side, supported by the three major UK parties, secured a 55% to 45% majority for Scotland to remain part of the United Kingdom. Following the result on 18 September 2014, Scotland\'s First Minister, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Salmond" title="Alex Salmond">Alex Salmond</a>, announced his intention to step down as First Minister and leader of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">SNP</a>. He was replaced by his deputy, <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Sturgeon" title="Nicola Sturgeon">Nicola Sturgeon</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Conservative_Government.2C_2015.E2.80.93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Conservative_Government,_2015\xe2\x80\x93present">Conservative Government, 2015\xe2\x80\x93present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Political_history_of_the_United_Kingdom_(1945%E2%80%93present)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Conservative Government, 2015\xe2\x80\x93present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="David_Cameron_.282015.E2.80.9316.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="David_Cameron_(2015\xe2\x80\x9316)">David Cameron (2015&#8211;16)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Political_history_of_the_United_Kingdom_(1945%E2%80%93present)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: David Cameron (2015\xe2\x80\x9316)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Second_Cameron_ministry" title="Second Cameron ministry">Second Cameron ministry</a></div>\n<p>After years of austerity, the British economy was on an upswing in 2015. In line with the Fixed Term Parliaments Act, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a> was called for 7 May 2015. The Conservatives claimed credit for the upswing, promising to keep taxes low and reduce the deficit as well as promising an In/Out referendum on the UK\'s relationship with the European Union. The rival Labour party called for a higher minimum wage, and higher taxes on the rich. In Scotland, the SNP attacked the austerity programme, opposed nuclear weapons and demanded that promises of more autonomy for Scotland made during the independence referendum be delivered.\n</p><p>Pre-election polls had predicted a close race and a hung parliament, but the surprising result was that a majority Conservative government was elected. The Conservatives with 37% of the popular vote held a narrow majority with 331 of the 650 seats. The other main victor was the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> which won 56 of the 59 seats in Scotland, a gain of 50. Labour suffered its worst defeat since 1987, taking only 31% of the votes and 232 seats; they lost 40 of their 41 seats in Scotland. The <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> vote fell by 2/3 and they lost 49 of their 57 seats, as their coalition with the Conservatives had alienated the great majority of their supporters. The new <a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">UK Independence Party</a> (UKIP), rallying voters against Europe and against immigration, did well with 13% of the vote count. It came in second in over 115 constituencies but came in first in only one. Women now comprise 29% of the MPs.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\nFollowing the election, the Leaders of the Labour Party and Liberal Democrats both resigned. They were replaced by <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Farron" title="Tim Farron">Tim Farron</a>, respectively.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Withdrawal_from_the_EU">Withdrawal from the EU</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Political_history_of_the_United_Kingdom_(1945%E2%80%93present)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Withdrawal from the EU">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg/220px-United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg.png" width="220" height="326" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg/330px-United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg/440px-United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="871" data-file-height="1289" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_EU_referendum_2016_area_results_2-tone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Results_of_the_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="Results of the United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">Results of the 2016 referendum</a> <span class="nowrap"><span style="background-color:#FFC010; color:black; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> Remain</span> <span class="nowrap"><span style="background-color:#0069B5; color:white; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> Leave</span></div></div></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small><i>(June 2017)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>On 23 June 2016, UK voters elected to withdraw from the European Union by a thin margin with 48% in favour of remaining, 52% in favour of leaving the European Union. London, Scotland, and Northern Ireland were three regions most in favour of the <a href="/wiki/Britain_Stronger_in_Europe" title="Britain Stronger in Europe">Remain vote</a>, while Wales and England\'s northern region were strongly <a href="/wiki/Vote_Leave" title="Vote Leave">pro-Leave</a>. Although he called for the referendum, British Prime Minister David Cameron had campaigned ardently for the Remain vote. He faced significant opposition from other parties on the right who came to view British membership in the EU as a detriment to the country\'s security and economic vitality. <a href="/wiki/UKIP" class="mw-redirect" title="UKIP">UKIP</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Farage" title="Nigel Farage">Nigel Farage</a> called the vote Britain\'s "independence day",<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> despite the fact that the UK was already an independent sovereign country.\n</p><p>Brexit had a <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_the_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="Aftermath of the United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">few immediate consequences</a>. Hours after the results of the referendum, David Cameron announced that he would resign as Prime Minister, claiming that "fresh leadership" was needed.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> In addition, because Scottish voters were highly in favour of remaining in the EU, Scotland\'s First Minister <a href="/wiki/Nicola_Sturgeon" title="Nicola Sturgeon">Nicola Sturgeon</a> announced that the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish government">Scottish government</a> would begin to organize <a href="/wiki/Proposed_second_Scottish_independence_referendum" title="Proposed second Scottish independence referendum">another referendum on the question of Scottish independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> On the economic side of things, the value of the British pound declined sharply after the results of the election were made clear. Stock markets in both Britain and New York were down the day after the referendum. Oil prices also fell.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Theresa_May_.282016.E2.80.93.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Theresa_May_(2016\xe2\x80\x93)">Theresa May (2016\xe2\x80\x93)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Political_history_of_the_United_Kingdom_(1945%E2%80%93present)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Theresa May (2016\xe2\x80\x93)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Premiership_of_Theresa_May" title="Premiership of Theresa May">Premiership of Theresa May</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/May_ministry_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="May ministry (disambiguation)">May ministry</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small><i>(June 2017)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)_leadership_election,_2016" title="Conservative Party (UK) leadership election, 2016">Conservative Party leadership election</a> occurred following Cameron\'s announcement of his resignation. All candidates except <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> had either been eliminated or withdrawn from the race by 11 July 2016; as a result, May automatically became the new <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Leader of the Conservative Party (UK)">Leader of the Conservative Party</a> and became the Prime Minister on 13 July. On 18 April 2017, the Prime Minister Theresa May announced she would seek an <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017" title="United Kingdom general election, 2017">election on 8 June</a><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>, despite previously ruling out an <a href="/wiki/Snap_election" title="Snap election">early election</a> on a multitude of occasions .<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>The outcome of the election resulted in the second hung parliament of the 21st century: with the conservatives being the largest party with 317 seats (which was 9 seats short of a majority).<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>This resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Conservative%E2%80%93DUP_agreement" title="Conservative\xe2\x80\x93DUP agreement">formation</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Minority_government" title="Minority government">minority conservative government</a> which was <a href="/wiki/Confidence_and_supply" title="Confidence and supply">supported</a> by the Northern Irish <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Unionist_Party" title="Democratic Unionist Party">Democratic Unionist Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Political_history_of_the_United_Kingdom_(1945%E2%80%93present)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul politics">British politics portal</a></span></li></ul></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Social_history_of_the_United_Kingdom_(1945%E2%80%93present)" title="Social history of the United Kingdom of England">Social history of England \xc2\xa7&#160;Since 1945</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Post%E2%80%93World_War_II_economic_expansion" title="Post\xe2\x80\x93World War II economic expansion">Post\xe2\x80\x93World War II economic expansion</a></li></ul>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Political_history_of_the_United_Kingdom_(1945%E2%80%93present)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46"
